<div id="review_64873101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64873101" />
    <a title="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten"><img alt="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305870184p2/2406353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64873101?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)" href="/user/show/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten">Rachel (The Rest Is Still Unwritten)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2406353-rachel-the-rest-is-still-unwritten?shelf=bought-by-me">bought-by-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer64873101&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64873101" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6534696671275271142">I really have mixed emotions about this book. Although i did enjoy it, there were times i felt that i wasn't really getting anywhere. While it eventually picked up pace towards the end, and then i couldn't put it down, i felt like Dru didn't really do a lot during the book. She either spent her time in her room, alone, or with Graves. <br/>I found i enjoyed the bits where Christophe was there the most. He gave the book a freshness that sometimes wasn't there. He made certain parts fun. I hope to see </span>
  <span id="freeText6534696671275271142" style="display:none">I really have mixed emotions about this book. Although i did enjoy it, there were times i felt that i wasn't really getting anywhere. While it eventually picked up pace towards the end, and then i couldn't put it down, i felt like Dru didn't really do a lot during the book. She either spent her time in her room, alone, or with Graves. <br />I found i enjoyed the bits where Christophe was there the most. He gave the book a freshness that sometimes wasn't there. He made certain parts fun. I hope to see him having a larger part in any future books.<br />To be perfectly honest, after the first book, going into this one i didn't really consider Christophe a real love interest for Dru.....but now? I'm not so sure. It's pretty obvious that Dru feels some sort of attraction towards him, although at times he scares her, and i really like how he acts towards her sometimes. He's very protective. However, then there's Graves.... and this is the part where i get really confused. <br />He's not what you'd usually expect of a male lead in a book. He's not exactly the most attractive guy (I know, i know. That sounded shallow to me-even as i wrote it, but it's true) and he's not always what you'd call 'cool', but he has his moments. Sometimes he'll say something really witty and funny, or do something really sweet and kind for Dru and i can totally imagine then as a couple. Then i think of Christophe. Each time Dru's with one of them, i am completely on their side, however then i switch teams when she's with the other. <br />Despite Dru being fairly sure it's Graves she wants to be with, i foresee a real love triangle popping up in future books.<br />Now.... onto other things lol. I really liked some of the new characters introduced. Dib's is a total sweetie and i'm interested to see just what exactly is in store for Ash. Why did he help Dru? Can he really be helped? Or is he a lost cause like Christophe thinks he is? <br />And Christophe? I was shocked to discover that he was Sergej's son. I did not expect that one, at all! I can't wait to discover just what he knows and what he's keeping to himself. <br /><br />**Now i just have to share this thought: <br />After Christophe had drank from Dru, Dibs mentioned that he hadn't drank enough for Dru to be at risk of bonding before Peter had shushed him- ending anything he'd been planning on saying. Then later on when Dru was accusing Christophe of betraying her mother he told her 'it isn't possible'. <br />What exactly is bonding? Is it something that just happens between djamhir's or can it happen to anyone? And is it possible that Christophe was bonded to Dru's mother?**<br />Question, questions, questions and i for one can't wait to have them answered. <br />Bring on the next book....and soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6534696671275271142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122549614" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122549614" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2664101-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298377267p2/2664101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122549614?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/2664101-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2664101-becky?shelf=read-for-review">read-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122549614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12260650309168540342">Betrayals is yet another kick-butt book from the awesome Lili St. Crow. Yes, it is true; I am becoming quite a fan of this series. <br/><br/><br/>The prologue of Betrayals reminds us how Strange Angels ended. This is definitely a series to read in the correct order. You’ll miss out on so much action-packed fun if you skip ahead. And indeed, if you read this review you will give yourself gigantic spoilers for the first book. You have been warned.<br/><br/><br/>For those of you still with me, we meet Dru again as she takes up </span>
  <span id="freeText12260650309168540342" style="display:none">Betrayals is yet another kick-butt book from the awesome Lili St. Crow. Yes, it is true; I am becoming quite a fan of this series. <br /><br /><br />The prologue of Betrayals reminds us how Strange Angels ended. This is definitely a series to read in the correct order. You’ll miss out on so much action-packed fun if you skip ahead. And indeed, if you read this review you will give yourself gigantic spoilers for the first book. You have been warned.<br /><br /><br />For those of you still with me, we meet Dru again as she takes up enforced residence at the Schola. She still has the feisty, crude and determined edge that defines her voice and character. So needless to say, she is far from happy when she gets put in the baby classes at the Schola, is prevented from training and is left out of all the supernatural action. Dru is miserable and the novel is structured around her being placed in a situation which is beyond her control. She spends hours in her room alone and brooding on her predicament and waiting for the impending doom to come.<br /><br /><br />Graves is perhaps even more adorable in this book. He doesn’t always keep Dru in the loop. Hey, do you like the pun? He is loup-garou...get it?! Anyway, he is such a dopey wolf-boy, almost like an obedient puppy except for the killer instinct (obviously) and he commands his supernatural abilities in this book. I also loved meeting other wulfen, their individuality really stood out and the affectionate relationship between them endeared them to me. <br /><br /><br />Christophe on the other hand is not my favourite character but he certainly adds an ever present sense of mystery and tension to the story. <br /><br /><br />I notice I have told you nothing of the plot. I think you can probably guess that Dru isn’t safe in the Schola though, right? So what more do you need to know? There is butt-kicking. It is exceedingly refreshing and fun.<br /><br /><br />I was reading Betrayals expecting not to like it as much as Strange Angels. You had all left me comments saying it wasn’t quite on a par. But you know, I have no idea what you lovely people were on about. I really enjoyed this book in equal measure to my love of the first. I can only assume that you didn’t like the fact that Dru wasn’t calling the shots in this book but please correct me if I’m wrong. I am certainly intrigued because I thought it was gripping, adrenalin-fuelled, angsty and high on melodrama. The only thing I would say is that all the different groupings are starting to confuse me a little bit: djamphir, Nosferatu, wampyr, wolfen, broken. I could do with a baby class on the breeding habits of the supernatural. That little niggle aside, I thought this was fabulous. I am so excited to start Jealously. A definite series addiction is developing here!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12260650309168540342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90484432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90484432" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2758899-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90484432?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/2758899-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer90484432&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90484432" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7511099195579702621">Man! I LOVED Betrayals! I thought Strange Angels was pretty good/descent...but Betrayals was incredible. I did not want to put this book down. My heart was racing right along with Dru's. St Crow does an absolute fabulous job of allowing the reader to relate to and empathize with Dru. She mixes the right amount of toughness and vulnerability to make these characters seem real, instead of the typical fearless, superhero type. I like how she shows the inward struggle Dru constantly faces over recen</span>
  <span id="freeText7511099195579702621" style="display:none">Man! I LOVED Betrayals! I thought Strange Angels was pretty good/descent...but Betrayals was incredible. I did not want to put this book down. My heart was racing right along with Dru's. St Crow does an absolute fabulous job of allowing the reader to relate to and empathize with Dru. She mixes the right amount of toughness and vulnerability to make these characters seem real, instead of the typical fearless, superhero type. I like how she shows the inward struggle Dru constantly faces over recent events (including her father's death) and her new surroundings. She lets us see Dru deal with the grief, the overwhelming change of everything, and the constant need to have someone she can trust and the loneliness of her situation. Dru is one of the most realistic characters that I have come across in this genre. I'm usually all for the hard-core heroines who show no weakness but I find that Dru's "weaknesses" are endearing and that much more relate-able...in the way she "leaks"...how she doesn't always have the answer...how she does need friends (she's not self-sufficient). I love that she's brave but still wants to feel the safeness of someone's (whether that someone is Graves or Christophe *wink, wink*) arms. I like what St Crow did with Graves in this one too. In Strange Angels, it was quite obvious he was going to be a contender for the love interest role and I hated it. He just didn't seem strong enough be with Dru and in her world. I find the whole dominant thing sexy, along with his loyalty and protective-vibe he has for Dru. <br />And what about Christophe? PLEASE DON'T LET HIM END UP BEING HER REAL FATHER!!! It's just so painfully obvious that there was something going on between him and her mother. Can someone tell me, was that a kiss for sure that "something soft and warm" that pressed against her mouth? Could this be explained any other way besides a kiss? Apart from this his behavior could be that of a protective father. Please someone prove me wrong!!! I will be devestated if I end up being right. I'm really cheering for Dru and Christophe being together. I guess I will just have to keep reading. July 29th can't come quick enough. <br />St Crox's ingenius writing is a perfect combination of keeping mysteries and unknowns with perfectly timed revelations and insights. With one answered question comes several unanswered ones and even though at times it was maddening it made this book irrestible. <br />If you liked Strange Angels then you will love Betrayals. If you're someone like me who wasn't absolutely blown away by Strange Angels give Betrayals a try...I can't imagine anyone being disappointed!!!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7511099195579702621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer73938800" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11935614581972570794">Dru Anderson's mother was killed, and now Dru's being hunted. The Schola is supposed to keep her safe, but in a place full of djamphir and werwulfen, "safe" is a relative term - especially considering there's an unknown traitor in the midst. Meanwhile, Dru's own powers are getting closer to "blooming", and she's been betrayed so many times she can no longer trust anyone - especially not herself.<br/><br/>The featured creatures in <u>Betrayals</u> are intriguingly disturbing, and bloody well creative, particularl</span>
  <span id="freeText11935614581972570794" style="display:none">Dru Anderson's mother was killed, and now Dru's being hunted. The Schola is supposed to keep her safe, but in a place full of djamphir and werwulfen, "safe" is a relative term - especially considering there's an unknown traitor in the midst. Meanwhile, Dru's own powers are getting closer to "blooming", and she's been betrayed so many times she can no longer trust anyone - especially not herself.<br /><br />The featured creatures in <u>Betrayals</u> are intriguingly disturbing, and bloody well creative, particularly the Broken. The lashings of Romanian words and phrases are deliciously exotic, and definitely welcome. I don't understand some things Christophe Reynard says, though, likely because Dru doesn't know, either. And the book would be easier to follow if it came with a glossary. There are some terms, and differences between them, that I don't quite understand, and a handy guide would be appreciated. eg. <i>svetocha</i>; differences between <i>djamphir</i>, <i>nosferatu</i> and Kouroi; differences between werwulfen and <i>loup-garou</i>; etc. I'm still not sure to what the Strange Angels series title is referring, and I'd guess the Ravelle, only they barely get a look-in here.<br /><br />Beware the cliff-hanger ending - Book 3, <u>Jealousy</u>, won't be published until 24th June 2010.<br /><br />P.S. Two thoughts Dru has in relation to Graves make me feel uncomfortable: <i>A flush crept up into his sallow cheeks. Under the Asian coloring he could really change it up.</i> Also, <i>Knelt down carefully, and I could see how pale he was under his ethnic coloring.</i> I may be overly PC, but these comments don't quite sit well with me. Then again, I'm white trash so my knowledge of race relations is probably lacking.<br /><br /><i>FTC Advisory: The Australian publisher provided me with an early copy of <u>Betrayals</u> in exchange for an unbiased review. No sponsorships or bribes were involved. If you click and order via the Buy links, I receive a tiny affiliate fee, and rarely generate enough to actually use the fee to spend on Amazon products. And not just because of the frightful cost of international postage.</i></span>

<div id="review_138070631" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138070631" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138070631?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-liked">books-i-liked</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138070631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16491081362748023928">Of the three books in this series thus far, I think Betrayals is my favourite. The story flow is not as slow as in the first book, there is a lot more action and the narration of Dru's inner feelings about both the boys in her life sounds convincingly like the thoughts of a tough-but-confused teenager.<br/><br/>However, all is not perfect, as is all too common these days. First off, Dru's still being irritatingly obtuse in this book, as also in the third one, so maybe it's a personality flaw I'm going to </span>
  <span id="freeText16491081362748023928" style="display:none">Of the three books in this series thus far, I think Betrayals is my favourite. The story flow is not as slow as in the first book, there is a lot more action and the narration of Dru's inner feelings about both the boys in her life sounds convincingly like the thoughts of a tough-but-confused teenager.<br /><br />However, all is not perfect, as is all too common these days. First off, Dru's still being irritatingly obtuse in this book, as also in the third one, so maybe it's a personality flaw I'm going to have to come to terms with. There are several instances when someone gives her a broad hint, or actually tells her about something, but she doesn't consider it, or realise the truth until it is spelt out for her in words of two syllables. Like for example, when Graves tells her that the Schola they're in is a reform school, and Christophe wonders why she was put in a school of this type, and she's still all like, a school of what type? Buy a clue, girl!<br /><br />And the author really needs to be a little less lazy about her re-tellings. Okay, I get that publishers want you to recap the previous books in a series so that a reader who picks up a book halfway through the series is not completely lost. But you can still retell the story in an interesting way, with different perspectives or something. Try to think of your loyal audience. Cutting and pasting entire scenes out of the previous book is just plain unacceptable, not to mention that it broke my concentration and made me annoyed enough to want to tear the pages out. I read all three books in a row, so I had to read about how Dru's mother protected her from the evil vampires three times in the exact same words! And about how Dru's dad became a zombie. And about her encounter with Sergej. Aaargh!<br /><br />But despite my ranting, I did like the book, quite a bit, so if you're sitting on the fence, I would tell you to jump on the side of reading, as opposed to not-reading Betrayals.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16491081362748023928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81975709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81975709" />
    <a title="Francis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1232443-francis"><img alt="Francis" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81975709?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Francis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Francis" href="/user/show/1232443-francis">Francis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81975709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13623434971822023144">I guess I would go 3.75 stars with this book. I liked it better than Strange Angels; I felt like more happened in this book than in the first one. In this book, Dru and Graves are placed in a Schola, ostensibly for their protection. But it rapidly becomes clear that Dru is not safe, and she has no idea who she can trust. I liked how this incarnation of the werwulf and nosferatu/dhjampir mythologies are fleshed out (particularly how the wulfen make consensus decisions in order to "hunt in packs")</span>
  <span id="freeText13623434971822023144" style="display:none">I guess I would go 3.75 stars with this book. I liked it better than Strange Angels; I felt like more happened in this book than in the first one. In this book, Dru and Graves are placed in a Schola, ostensibly for their protection. But it rapidly becomes clear that Dru is not safe, and she has no idea who she can trust. I liked how this incarnation of the werwulf and nosferatu/dhjampir mythologies are fleshed out (particularly how the wulfen make consensus decisions in order to "hunt in packs"), though there seemed to be almost nothing about the rest of the Real World in this book. (Presumably more is coming in future books). We find out some big reveals about the dhjampir Christophe, and Ash the werwulf comes back in several interesting ways. Dru's emotional isolation and claustrophobia are palpable, and I felt pulled in to see what happens next. There's talk about how she's the big hope of the Order, since as a female "svetocha", she will become toxic to vampires when she blooms (assuming she lives that long). Her relationships to the two boys in her life continue to be explored, as she learns more about the enigmatic Christophe, and Graves matures and begins to find his alpha-male place among the wulfen as a "loup-garou".<br /><br />There were a few infelicities; as in the first book, I found some places where the writing was unclear enough that I actually couldn't quite figure out what happened. There were also some "quotables" like "A warm car never stays warm for long. Heat is like love. It drains away." that seemed like they were kind of thrown in to make Dru sound more profound, but I'm not sure they had the intended effect.<br /><br />I suspect a Polish dictionary might increase one's enjoyment of the book a bit, as Christophe tosses in several terms of endearment at various places.<br /><br />It was good enough that I'm waiting eagerly for book 3, "Jealousy", in June 2010.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13623434971822023144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78318382" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78318382" />
    <a title="Tynga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2472291-tynga"><img alt="Tynga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397411073p2/2472291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78318382?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tynga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tynga" href="/user/show/2472291-tynga">Tynga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78318382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1714579378742363605">Fast-paced, action-packed, full of mystery and hidden secrets, you won't be able to put that book down!<br/>Betrayals is the second engagement in the Strange Angels series and while I liked the first book, I LOVED the second book.<br/><br/>First book ends when Dru gets to the Schola and the second books picks where we left off, Dru is in a Schola full of delinquent djamphir and wulfen teenage boys, and even though Christophe promised she would be safe there, something is wrong.<br/><br/><br/>Teachers won't let her learn figh</span>
  <span id="freeText1714579378742363605" style="display:none">Fast-paced, action-packed, full of mystery and hidden secrets, you won't be able to put that book down!<br />Betrayals is the second engagement in the Strange Angels series and while I liked the first book, I LOVED the second book.<br /><br />First book ends when Dru gets to the Schola and the second books picks where we left off, Dru is in a Schola full of delinquent djamphir and wulfen teenage boys, and even though Christophe promised she would be safe there, something is wrong.<br /><br /><br />Teachers won't let her learn fighting tactics, they won't teach her and explain her anything about the whole wulfen/djamphir/suckers/svetocha community and she finds it rather odd.<br />This book is all about mysteries and lies, secrets from the past and.. betrayals =P<br /><br /><br />I was really pleased with the characters in that book, Strange Angel kinda fell short for me in that department, but not this time around! Christopher is awesome, even though he isn't present very often he always makes a big impression. The wulfen and djamphir boys also have very interesting personalities, and different opinions and reactions toward Dru. Also Graves grows a lot in that book, he really isn't the skinny goth-boy anymore while Dru loose her tough girl facade to reveal a wounded and scared girl.<br /><br /><br />I had a very hard time put the book down because you really want to know more, and even after finishing the book I still feel that way. My questions aren't answered and it's killing me!<br />I want to know what's the entire deal with Christophe, how does he relate to Dru's mom? What's going on within the order? Why is Dru so special? Hopefully Jealousy (June 2010) will answer those questions!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1714579378742363605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1664789601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664789601" />
    <a title="Roxy the Fury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17729734-roxy-the-fury"><img alt="Roxy the Fury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443747889p2/17729734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664789601?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxy the Fury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxy the Fury" href="/user/show/17729734-roxy-the-fury">Roxy the Fury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17729734-roxy-the-fury?shelf=to-read-via-lib">to-read-via-lib</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664789601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9581843895686490417">It was very upsetting to find a great book with a kick ass heroine and then move on to book two and said heroine is a dud. Dru was depressed this whole entire book. I mean poke out my eyeballs depressing. I had to read this book in bits and pieces just so that I wouldn't get depressed. In book one, Dru kicked butt. She was trained by her father for just about anything. In this book? Dru was a lost little girl waiting for her knight in shining armor. What. The. Hell. Happened? This whole book sho</span>
  <span id="freeText9581843895686490417" style="display:none">It was very upsetting to find a great book with a kick ass heroine and then move on to book two and said heroine is a dud. Dru was depressed this whole entire book. I mean poke out my eyeballs depressing. I had to read this book in bits and pieces just so that I wouldn't get depressed. In book one, Dru kicked butt. She was trained by her father for just about anything. In this book? Dru was a lost little girl waiting for her knight in shining armor. What. The. Hell. Happened? This whole book shouldn't have even been written. Nothing and I mean nothing happened. Let me give you a quick summary of the book:<br /><br />Dru gets to the dark, dark Schola and skips class everyday because she's depressed. Graves suddenly gets hawt and he's the big Alpha on campus. Dru feels lost and doesn't know who to trust. She cries all the time, picks fights and doesn't finish them and climbs the roof. Yup. Climbs the roof and feels free. But then she doesn't. The depression comes back. Then Christophe comes in the picture and now there's some weird triangle between Graves and Dru and Christophe. But Christophe might have been in love with Dru's mom and now he's interested in Dru? Gross. They escape the Schola and Christophe takes them to another Schola. Annnnnnnd The End. That's. It. <br /><br />That's the book. Dru runs into fires and Dru runs into vampires and Dru does the stupidest things because quite honestly I think Dru is suicidal. This is a YA book people. With a suicidal almost(!) vamp that leaves valuable things behind and keeps waiting to be saved. <br /><br />Book one had great potential. Book two should be burned and forgotten. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9581843895686490417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69851842" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69851842" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2696686-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414955181p2/2696686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69851842?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/2696686-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2696686-katie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69851842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3223030374764235466">Following the supernatural-filled pages of Strange Angels, Betrayals was the perfect second addition to the series. It’s witty, action-packed and the plot opens a can of worms that will have you on the edge of your seat.<br/><br/>I didn’t enjoy it quite as much as I did Strange Angels. For a good chunk of the time I spent reading, it felt more like a filler book- something to add between main conflicts and plot changes. But regardless, it held the same attitude and boldness that the first one had.<br/><br/>Dru comp</span>
  <span id="freeText3223030374764235466" style="display:none">Following the supernatural-filled pages of Strange Angels, Betrayals was the perfect second addition to the series. It’s witty, action-packed and the plot opens a can of worms that will have you on the edge of your seat.<br /><br />I didn’t enjoy it quite as much as I did Strange Angels. For a good chunk of the time I spent reading, it felt more like a filler book- something to add between main conflicts and plot changes. But regardless, it held the same attitude and boldness that the first one had.<br /><br />Dru complained a lot in this one, but it was justified considering the circumstances. I was heavily bothered by her wishy-washy emotions towards Graves and Christophe though. She’s angry at Graves for not spending time for her and the next minute she‘s over it. She’s gushing about how strange and safe Christophe makes her feel and the next minute she‘s terrified of him. (And even though I’ll probably be skinned alive for this- I’m totally team Christophe. Graves just feels like a best friend to me, since that’s how he’s written.)<br /><br />I love how it ended. It took you right back to square one, with the exception of a few new, extra characters. Overall, if you were a fan of the first book- Strange Angels- this one will definitely not disappoint you. It’s not as engaging and fast-paced as the first one, but it’ll keep you turning the page.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3223030374764235466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gPaDpkNMLU1XTrgO/JFZ3jfC5iEPgO/y68uxTj8TBwMJimT/fZlKRJR2Kz2qoetZx1j/P6/MwS4KM22sJDweFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1xbH1Hq+05536KTU5Q6ZhG9u27stIbP0E+tSFh7r+WteaiCNRGu0l7TQN+ezPisDn/TCpY1tnSjyE470BcTgfA==')})
  }
